<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_db54d7cd-4e15-4e11-a9de-10fb669d634b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer8726594946690575144">Fourteen-year-old Maximum Ride, better known as Max, knows what it’s like to soar above the world. She and all the members of the “flock”—Fang, Iggy, Nudge, Gasman and Angel—are just like ordinary kids—only they have wings and can fly.   <span id="freeText8726594946690575144" style="display:none">Fourteen-year-old Maximum Ride, better known as Max, knows what it’s like to soar above the world. She and all the members of the “flock”—Fang, Iggy, Nudge, Gasman and Angel—are just like ordinary kids—only they have wings and can fly. It may seem like a dream come true to some, but their lives can morph into a living nightmare at any time... like when Angel, the youngest member of the flock, is kidnapped and taken back to the “School” where she and the others were experimented on by a crew of wack jobs. <br /><br />Her friends brave a journey to blazing hot Death Valley, CA, to save Angel, but soon enough, they find themselves in yet another nightmare—this one involving fighting off the half-human, half-wolf “Erasers” in New York City. Whether in the treetops of Central Park or in the bowels of the Manhattan subway system, Max and her adopted family take the ride of their lives. Along the way Max discovers from her old friend and father-figure Jeb—now her betrayed and greatest enemy—that her purpose is save the world—but can she?</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1834446174" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1834446174" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1834446174?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834446174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13651662032931342533">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>Not very long ago, I read the first novel in the MAXIMUM RIDE series and quite enjoyed the action, characters and story. But, as I was reading it, I kept wondering what it would be like to *see* this series.<br/><br/>So we sadly don’t have a TV show of this, but we do have a manga series (and a badly rated digital movie).<br/><br/>And it’s pretty damn exceptional.<br/><br/>Fortunately, there aren’t huge changes made to the plot at all. It’s still about Angel being kidnapped and Max and her crew going to rescue her,</span>
  <span id="freeText13651662032931342533" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />Not very long ago, I read the first novel in the MAXIMUM RIDE series and quite enjoyed the action, characters and story. But, as I was reading it, I kept wondering what it would be like to *see* this series.<br /><br />So we sadly don’t have a TV show of this, but we do have a manga series (and a badly rated digital movie).<br /><br />And it’s pretty damn exceptional.<br /><br />Fortunately, there aren’t huge changes made to the plot at all. It’s still about Angel being kidnapped and Max and her crew going to rescue her, but stumbling across/being followed by tons of Erasers.<br /><br />The only major thing that I felt changed from novel to manga was Fang. In the novel, he seemed… almost bestial. Not at all friendly. Yet, in the manga, we see him smile quite a few times and care about Max quite a bit. He didn’t seem unfriendly at all.<br /><br />You have no idea how good it was to be able to put a face to these characters, especially since there are a good couple of them. Granted, the majority look like dolls in the manga, which probably could have at least been a little more prevented, but Narae Lee drew them with originality still.<br /><br />And she draws such beautiful/life-like backgrounds. <br /><br />I breezed through this manga. It’s action-packed, interesting, emotional and so easy to get lost in.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13651662032931342533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2496784472" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2496784472?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2018</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=anime">anime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2496784472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9651388232558435610">I've never been a huge fan of the <i>Maximum Ride</i> series personally for a number of reasons, mainly the far-fetched plot and the cheesy dialogue, but there's something interesting to be said for a group of teenagers with the ability to fly like birds. Very similar to Stephen King's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233667.Firestarter' title='Firestarter by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Firestarter</a> with the experiment run amok and the evil shady government research lab, this massive story has a variety of characters with their own individual personalities, and with little info regarding their own identi</span>
  <span id="freeText9651388232558435610" style="display:none">I've never been a huge fan of the <i>Maximum Ride</i> series personally for a number of reasons, mainly the far-fetched plot and the cheesy dialogue, but there's something interesting to be said for a group of teenagers with the ability to fly like birds. Very similar to Stephen King's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/233667.Firestarter" title="Firestarter by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Firestarter</a> with the experiment run amok and the evil shady government research lab, this massive story has a variety of characters with their own individual personalities, and with little info regarding their own identity, they consider themselves a family of sorts - a bit dysfunctional, but a family just the same.<br /><br />This manga adaptation adds something new to the story with beautiful illustrations that really bring out the scenery and action of the novel basis. If there's one thing that can be said for this, it's a work of art and paints these avian kids almost like superheroes as they try to avoid being discovered and captured again, taken back to the "school" where they're basically used as guinea pigs (or in their case since they're part bird, guinea fowl? ...Sorry). For readers who dislike the thought of reading the large <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6885957.The_Angel_Experiment__Maximum_Ride___1_" title="The Angel Experiment (Maximum Ride, #1) by James Patterson" rel="nofollow noopener">Angel Experiment</a> book which the graphic novel is based upon, this might be a simpler place to start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9651388232558435610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robbie" href="/user/show/1197637-robbie">Robbie</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45861800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14784403692542692788">I have to review this both in relation to the original, and by its own. Tough!<br/><br/>Anyway, the story is still amazing and captivating, so points there. <br/><br/>It's an American original manga that they hired a Korean to write. It is definitely MANGA and not GRAPHIC NOVEL, especially considering it was serialized first in Yen Magazine. However, it does read left to right. <br/><br/>I feel like a little bit of the internal feelings/thinking is lost in this version over the original, which is interesting because many Jap</span>
  <span id="freeText14784403692542692788" style="display:none">I have to review this both in relation to the original, and by its own. Tough!<br /><br />Anyway, the story is still amazing and captivating, so points there. <br /><br />It's an American original manga that they hired a Korean to write. It is definitely MANGA and not GRAPHIC NOVEL, especially considering it was serialized first in Yen Magazine. However, it does read left to right. <br /><br />I feel like a little bit of the internal feelings/thinking is lost in this version over the original, which is interesting because many Japanese manga have quite a bit of internal thought. The emphasis on this version of Maximum Ride is definitely fast-paced action sequences, which it does well. <br /><br />The character designs are all very good, and distinctly Japanese-manga-y. I especially like Max and Iggy, who look older than I imagined and both got super sexy. Fang looks off to me, and Nudge looks like a ganguro girl, but whatever ^_^<br /><br />Definitely a good adaptation in its own right, it loses some of the charm but keeps all the appeal of the original.<br /><br />3 Quality, 5 Popularity</span>
  <a data-text-id="14784403692542692788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272177133?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anzuai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anzuai" href="/user/show/7617139-anzuai">Anzuai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7617139-anzuai?shelf=manga-sci-fi">manga-sci-fi</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272177133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1425190226342989179">Ok, let me first say something: I picked up this book knowing nothing about it, and because I was desperate to read something new. And I absolutely loved it!<br/> This is the manga version of the original book for Young Adults (mainly) by James Patterson, and it's very skillfully transformed into the new format. Excellent art, brilliant dialogue and characters so real you feel they might just jump off the page!<br/> Before I go into a bit more detail, if you're thinking of buying this book then DO IT!! Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText1425190226342989179" style="display:none">Ok, let me first say something: I picked up this book knowing nothing about it, and because I was desperate to read something new. And I absolutely loved it!<br /> This is the manga version of the original book for Young Adults (mainly) by James Patterson, and it's very skillfully transformed into the new format. Excellent art, brilliant dialogue and characters so real you feel they might just jump off the page!<br /> Before I go into a bit more detail, if you're thinking of buying this book then DO IT!! Buy it NOW! You won't be able to put it down, the plot keeps your on the edge of your seat the whole way through. I read it all in one sitting!<br /><br />**WARNING, SPOILERS AHEAD!!!**<br />The main character, Max, is a great lead. She's super cool, and really appeals to a teenage reader. The story starts off with her dreaming about people chasing her, and in her dream she has wings. This part (if you have the same version as me) is done in colour, which is a great start to the book. After she wakes up, we're introduced to the rest of the gang; Gazzy, Angel, Fang, Nudge and Iggy, who all have various and wonderful talents. <br /> The main twist in the plot (stop reading now if you haven't read it yet!) is the arrival of the Erasers, terrifying wolf-like creatures who are led by Jeb's son Ari. Their arrival is drawn over a double-page spread, which draws the reader directly into the suspense. After kidnapping Angel, they fly off and take her to the School, a place where Jeb freed the others from years ago. <br /> I'm not going to go into much more detail about this plot, because it's fairly self-explainitory, Max and the others plan to rescure Angel and run into mysteries about the Erasers, Ari, their parents and Jeb himself along the way. <br /> The book ends with a cliffhanger (I'm not saying what it is) which made me yell "Wait, say WHAT!!" ^_^' <br /><br />I'm going to end my review with a simple list of why you should get this book: 1. Brilliant characters 2. Stunning art 3. An involving and fast-paced, action packed plotline!<br /><br />Enjoy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1425190226342989179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5972221908327505843" style="display:none">Wow. That's all I can say about this book.<br />I had put it on hod at the library and went over to pick it up along with the second book, since I couldn't get my hands on the chapter book yet, and man am I happy that I picked it up.<br /><br />This series has everything - a refreshing cast of characters that are funny and adventurous and all those other things that other characters lack, and for once, they are realistic, not cliche like Bella and Edward and the whole crappy cast from Twilight is. The art is great to look at and I truly feel like I'm reading a manga book, not a cheap excuse for a manga like a few books I have read were like. <br /><br />The theme of this series actually reminds me of my own book I'm writing because there are some similiar details, especially cause my main character also has wings. But enough about that.<br /><br />I can now tell why this series is so popular. Looking forward to enjoy the rest of it</span>

<div id="review_2758895955" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2758895955" />
    <a title="Laura L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24590983-laura-l"><img alt="Laura L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591123086p2/24590983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2758895955?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura L" href="/user/show/24590983-laura-l">Laura L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099538363" href="/book/show/6720495-maximum-ride">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24590983-laura-l?shelf=just-okay-3-stars">just-okay-3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24590983-laura-l?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24590983-laura-l?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2758895955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15302547378445731665">This is an interesting adaption. I've read the whole maximum ride series of novels, this is my first time reading one of the graphic novels. The regular novels I think are better, there's more detail to the characters and plot, and they take more than one hour to read. <br/><br/>There were some errors in the panels, I know that lots of graphic novels have errors but, none that I have really noticed enough to bother my reading experience. This book had a couple of errors that bothered me, the main one bein</span>
  <span id="freeText15302547378445731665" style="display:none">This is an interesting adaption. I've read the whole maximum ride series of novels, this is my first time reading one of the graphic novels. The regular novels I think are better, there's more detail to the characters and plot, and they take more than one hour to read. <br /><br />There were some errors in the panels, I know that lots of graphic novels have errors but, none that I have really noticed enough to bother my reading experience. This book had a couple of errors that bothered me, the main one being on one of the last pages where Angel's face was drawn over the bars of her cage. <br /><br />I won't be continuing the graphic novel adaption of this series, I saw the first volume at the library and decided to check it out.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer2312789870881071633">I read the book version of this manga about 20 years ago, before James Patterson was a big kahuna. I was still in high school, had never heard of dystopian lit, rarely read sci-fi, and found the idea pretty awesome. I haven't read the manga until now because it's just been on my radar but the length of the series intimidated me--such a big commitment.<br/><br/>I finally picked up the series for my son, who is resistant to reading anything new. When he refused to read them, I started on book 1. I read it i</span>
  <span id="freeText2312789870881071633" style="display:none">I read the book version of this manga about 20 years ago, before James Patterson was a big kahuna. I was still in high school, had never heard of dystopian lit, rarely read sci-fi, and found the idea pretty awesome. I haven't read the manga until now because it's just been on my radar but the length of the series intimidated me--such a big commitment.<br /><br />I finally picked up the series for my son, who is resistant to reading anything new. When he refused to read them, I started on book 1. I read it in a day or two, completely absorbed. The story is fantastic, and the characters shine. I really enjoyed it, though there were definitely parts where I felt like things were missing that would be explained in the regular novel. But for an adaptation, it's one of the better ones I've read. I'm in for the long haul--next 8 books, here I come!<br /><br />Also, I convinced my son that the books were great and he is now on book 3! :D</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_805842548" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/805842548" />
    <a title="N.T. Embe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5395467-n-t-embe"><img alt="N.T. Embe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537744425p2/5395467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/805842548?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="N.T. Embe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="N.T. Embe" href="/user/show/5395467-n-t-embe">N.T. Embe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of James Patterson's works and people who don't mind very little depth to their reads.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to N.T. by: </span>
      Barnes and Noble
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer805842548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15816190270830444594"><br/>I remember when I first picked up this manga, my interest was raised by the title. It's an unusual one, to be certain, and once I looked at the cover, I fell in love with the dynamic art style and beautiful coloration of the art. I remember flipping it open in the Barnes and Noble and reading through the first few pages before I realized I was actually <i>reading</i> the book already. It flew by, a light and easy read without too much thought and the most basic of content, especially as far as reading </span>
  <span id="freeText15816190270830444594" style="display:none"><br />I remember when I first picked up this manga, my interest was raised by the title. It's an unusual one, to be certain, and once I looked at the cover, I fell in love with the dynamic art style and beautiful coloration of the art. I remember flipping it open in the Barnes and Noble and reading through the first few pages before I realized I was actually <i>reading</i> the book already. It flew by, a light and easy read without too much thought and the most basic of content, especially as far as reading material goes.<br /><br />Re-reading this manga again, perhaps that first basic decision to read it based on its superficial appeal was a herald of things to come. And yet as much as I can say that, I can also say that I enjoyed reading this manga.<br /><br />But be forewarned: It's stripped to the barest of bones.<br /><br />Being a book-to-manga conversion, which I found out a little while after having read the manga the first time, I would assume that's much of the reason for why this series is so threadbare on content. The art style is beautiful and enchanting, and I can't help but eat it up eagerly. But as far as plot, storyline, twists-and-turns, and most of the basics to any literature go, reading this manga is definitely like receiving the skeleton of a piece rather than anything close to a whole person.<br /><br />This manga suffers from very little plot, very little character development or explanation, and keeps me reading simply because you can literally fly through this without taking a moment to think--at all! There's no brainpower needed to read this, because there's barely any content to read besides the most basic of storylines which is what we receive.<br /><br />Now this does not mean that I don't enjoy the content or the concepts introduced therein, but I suspect, as I've mentioned, that this manga series is suffering from severe downsizing since it had been taken from book form to manga form. I will say this with an air of caution, however, because I have never read any of James Patterson's works before, and so I cannot say if there is more content to his actual book series than there is to this manga version. But it's a consideration to take into account. If you're a fan of James Patterson or this series, then I'm sure you'll find this a refreshing and beautifully illustrated version of the books.<br /><br /><br />Overall, I cannot say that this is a series that everyone will love. Possibly because of the minimal content, people might find this a boring read. In my case, I enjoyed the read. It's fast-paced and very easy to fly through these volumes, and some depth does seem to begin developing by the next volume, but it definitely might not be the right cup of tea for everyone. Still, because it's a quick and easy read, if you're looking for something light to breeze through, I would say to give this series a shot.<br /><br /><br />I'll be reading more of this series as I can find it in my library. So until the next time, enjoy your reading, everyone!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15816190270830444594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_94237166" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94237166" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2465264-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503933667p2/2465264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94237166?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/2465264-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=comic">comic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2465264-donna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94237166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9034352404535143142">This was my first manga book and it will probably be my last (except for the Labyrinth ones, I'm still seriously considering getting those). First, can someone please tell me how 'manga' is pronounced? I keep saying it like the Italian word for 'eat.' I've also pronounced pilates like pee-lats because I'd never heard it pronounced before. Can someone help me out here?<br/><br/>The thing is, I don't know what's normal for manga and what isn't. It's not like reading a comic book/graphic novel. I like comics</span>
  <span id="freeText9034352404535143142" style="display:none">This was my first manga book and it will probably be my last (except for the Labyrinth ones, I'm still seriously considering getting those). First, can someone please tell me how 'manga' is pronounced? I keep saying it like the Italian word for 'eat.' I've also pronounced pilates like pee-lats because I'd never heard it pronounced before. Can someone help me out here?<br /><br />The thing is, I don't know what's normal for manga and what isn't. It's not like reading a comic book/graphic novel. I like comics. I enjoy them. But this was just weird. For instance, is it normal to have a characters actions spelled out around them (like when a character was shaking, 'shake' was actually written around the character)? I just found that annoying.<br /><br />I also found the drawings really distracting, probably because they were really detracting from the plot, which was hard to follow because there were more drawings than plot-related words. I had a hard time catching onto the plot because I felt it was buried under the pictures. Every once in a while I'd grasp hold of it and like what I was reading but then I'd lose it again. It'd just get buried underneath all the busy artwork, which I don't even really like. I've always been kind of freaked out by manga-style drawings (way too angular) so that didn't help the book's cause any.<br /><br />This was another BEA random grab that has taught me to be way more selective about the books I nab this time around. I just saw 'James Patterson' and pretty colors and yoink! Not again.<br /><br />In all honesty, I can't tell if I liked the story. From what I've gathered of the plot it's not bad. It doesn't sound too much like my thing to read but I've heard good reviews of it. But I'll have to read the actual novels to really find out. So consider this review based purely on the manga aspect of it and not on James Patterson's work. It's safe to say I'm not a manga fan and I won't be picking it up again any time soon (unless it's Labyrinth, I might just suck it up for that). I'll leave this one to the real manga fans out there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9034352404535143142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2128060926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2128060926" />
    <a title="Toni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64217016-toni"><img alt="Toni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605901666p2/64217016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2128060926?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toni" href="/user/show/64217016-toni">Toni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64217016-toni?shelf=manga-and-graphic-novels">manga-and-graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64217016-toni?shelf=library-checkouts">library-checkouts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64217016-toni?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2128060926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18434448357690090574">Maximum Ride is one of those rare cases where I can truthfully say I prefer an adaptation to the source material. Patterson's writing in the original series is godawful - terse, basic, and stuffed with cliches and contrived plot-holes to the point of bursting - and conveys details horribly, but the graphic novel eliminated enough of the issues I had with the books to be considered enjoyable by my standards. I love NaRae Lee's art style, too, and I think it complemented the story quite well. (Of </span>
  <span id="freeText18434448357690090574" style="display:none">Maximum Ride is one of those rare cases where I can truthfully say I prefer an adaptation to the source material. Patterson's writing in the original series is godawful - terse, basic, and stuffed with cliches and contrived plot-holes to the point of bursting - and conveys details horribly, but the graphic novel eliminated enough of the issues I had with the books to be considered enjoyable by my standards. I love NaRae Lee's art style, too, and I think it complemented the story quite well. (Of course, the story itself suffers from certain overdone tropes, especially in personalities; however, I didn't find them to be as noticeable here.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18434448357690090574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n/bcpOvr8BX7JVbxuToouaXGW+yWGUPOJspSTzVPJ0iJXWSZQDO2z5O3cVNxCjA5kdLgPKMC2FEUt76zZz2qHQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OySiIvkiV7PC1yRTzoJyFE7YmionvgT2BQf5kk+P9r0tjxofUvoRaapFA/EGsmqUeswh+hKln2k3ehVuHf176A==')})
  }

It's a lot to live up to, but NaRae proved to be up to the challenge by delivering artwork that looks remarkably polished for a relative newbie to the world of international manga publishing. </span>
